MISS RAYMOND IS TRUE.
Prefers a Black-Face Artist to a
Wealthy Stock Broker.
Rumor was busy last night in regard to
a forthcoming marriage between the
handsome, dashing vocalist. Miss I,izzie
Raymond, and Mr. Montgomery of Mont
gomery & Stone, the black face team.
Miss Raymond, who closes an engage
ment in this city to-morrow evening, was
asked about her marriage, and said:
"I am not married to Mr. Montgom
ery."
"Do you intend to marry him?"
"I certainly do, as I am engaged to
him," was the reply. "I shall soon go
East to marry him. He opens in St.
Louis Sunday evening. I told him when
he left here not to worry, as I would
surely keep my word, notwithstanding
the persistent offer of marriage from :%.
wealthy Boston stock broker, who I find
is rated 'way up in G' by Bradstreet. I
know that with Montgomery the course
of true love will run smooth, and hence it
is all off with the broker."
"What is the broker's name?"
"I shall not tell you, as I do not wish
to wound his generous heart. It's lovo
that I want, not money, and I know that
Montgomery loves me dearly."
In the Divorce Courts
Judge Bahrs has granted Rosa A. Carr
a divorce from Charles Carr on the
ground of infidelity.
Maud A. Brutz has been granted a di
vorce from Clifford J. Brutz on the
ground of desertion.
Judge Hebbard yesterday granted W.
J. Smith a divorce from Margaret Smith
on the ground of habitual intemperance.
William O. Baldwin has commenced suit
for divorce against Minerva Baldwin on
the ground of cruelty.

ASSAULTED
BY THE MAN
SHE LOVED
Etta Murray, a Young
Woman, Danger
ously 111.
Attacked by Mike Valve
and Seriously In
jured.
Her Assailant, Fearing Arrest,
Quietly Leaves the
City.
THE POLICE ARE NOTIFIED
Threatened to Kill Her If She Told
Her Parents of His
Crime.
Etta Mm-ray, an attractive young
woman, Is lying- dangerous 111 at her
mother's home, 604 Third street. Last
Tuesday night, she claims, she was as
saulted by Mike Valve, a. young man
with whom she had kept company.
According to her story Valve entered
her home during the temporary ab
sence of her mother and assaulted her.
She screamed for help, but her alleged
assailant placed his hand over her
mouth and threatened to kill her if she
continued to make an outcry. After he
had accomplished his design he left the
house after threatening to return a.nd
make her a subject for the Coroner if
she informed her mother.
When the latter returned several
hours, later she found her daughter ly
ing on the floor in a semi-conscious
condition. She at once sent for a doc
tor, who after considerable trouble suc
ceeded in reviving the injured girl. Af
ter regaining consciousness she told her
mother what had transpired.
Mrs. Murray lost no time in notifying
the police, and two detectives were sent
to make an investigation. They ob
tained the story of the girl, and at
once started out to find her allege! as
sailant. They visited his residence on
Broadway but were unable to find him.
An examination of his room disclosed
that he had taken his clothes.
Last nlerht the detectives learned that
Valve, evidently fearing: arrest, had left
the city. He was traced to Stockton,
and Sheriff Cunningham of that place
was notified by telegraph to arrest him. â 
Cunningham, after making 1 an investi
gation, telegraphed back to Chief Lees
that Valve had left that city.
A description of him has been pent
to the various Sheriffs throughout the
country and every effort will be made
to arrest him.
Late last nigrht it was reported that
the frirl was in a dyinjr condition and
could not possibly recover. Her mother
is heartbroken over the condition of the
unfortunate girl and is determined to
prosecute Valve to the bitter end In
case he is arrested. She was aware that
he was in the habit of oallinc on her
dauerht^r. hut thinking that he intend
ed to make her his wife she offered no
objection. He evidently knew that
Mrs. Murray was absent when he en
tered her house Tuesday nleht. After
ealnine an entrance, it is claimed, he
struck his unsuspecting victim, felling
her to the floor, before accomplishing
his base dÂ» c iern.
The police are determined to make
Valve suffer for his heinous crime and
will do all In their power to apprehend
him.
KOSTER STAYED AWAY.
An Evening's Sport Spoiled by the
Mission Pugilist Not Appearing
to Fight Lynch.
About five hundred disappointed sport*
filled the gymnasium of the Excelsior
Athletic Club last night, watching two
wild-eyed colored "dubs" wave their
hands at each other until one fell to the
floor in a hypnotized condition.
The event that crowded the clubroom
was an eight-round go between Tom
Lynch of the Excelsiors and Ous Koster
of the Manhattan*, At the last moment
Koster "crawfished," as one sport put it,
and the go waa called off. To satisfy
the gore-loving followers of the squared
circle the management substituted Henry
Lewis and young Peter Jackson, two
dusky "dubs." As was expected, Lewis
went to the floor to save a beating, while
the crowd wondered why he stayed that
length of time. Jackson was a power
ful fellow, with as much knowledge of
boxing as a Spaniard has of fighting.
Lewis, on the other hand, had some
knowledge of the game, but is totally
devoid of courage. With two such men
in the ring the crowd simply lay back
and yawned, waiting for the bout to be
over. It came in the fourth round and
no onÂ© felt sorry.
The events that preceded the farce were
Interesting and partly made up for the
rank go. "Deacon" Jones and "Clown"
Wiley created merriment at the start by
their mode of sparring. Devlne and Mc-
Deavltt also boxed three laughable
rounds, while Jimmy Lawler and Jimmy
Rlelly, Craig and Lynch, O'Brien and
Kane boxed interesting rounds. Will Sul
livan contortioned and Mr. Casey warbled
the Wabash so realistically that the
spectators nearly drowned him with ap
plause. He then gave a pathetic reci
tation about an Indian who deserted his
love in the far West. His gestures were
a left lead for the stomach with right
hand in pocket: sometimes changing to
a right cross for variety. â¢ Casey was so
enraptured with his own voice that he
forgot his lines, and had to retire amid
tumultoua applause. Lynch and Ken
nedy then boxed four lively rounds.
In announcing the absence of Koster
President Kennedy charged Ale 6 Greg
gains with trying to put his club on the
"bum" because they were getting pros
perous. He defied the referee in the
Sharkey-Joffrios bout and all his "push"
to injure the Excelsiors, and then an
nounced another bout, which wilt tak*
place at the clubrooms in a few weeks.
Willie Dirks. Charley Priest and Wil
liam Perry are to appear before the San
Francisco Athletic Club on 'Wednesday
evening next In a lightweight tourna
ment.
Endeavorers and the War.
At a meeting of the executive commit
tee of Golden Gate Union last night the
lookout committee reported that it had
arranged for a farewell service to be held
at the Presidio Sunday morning at 11
o'clock. Addresses will be made by vet
eran chaplains and music will be fur
nished by the Presidio band. It has also
been ascertained that the State Endeav
orers will co-operate with the Red Uross
Society in furnishing comfort bags to
both soldiers and sailors, and the Ameri
can Tract Society will ship a quantity of
literature to lighten the Idle moments of
the boys on th*lr way to the front.
A Shoemaker Drowned.
Thp body of an unknown drowned man
was found floating in the bay at the foot
of Beale street wharf yesterday morning.
The deceased was about 35 years old and
was dressed as a laborer. On his person
was found an account book with the

Another Burglar Convicted.
Ray Bernal, who broke into a rooming-
House at the corner of Howard and Sixth
streets on March 24 last, and stole a
suit of clothes belonging to C. F. Gilles
r>ie was convicted of burglary in the
iwcond degree yesterday by a jury in

Bitten by a Spider.
Oliver Reese, living at 768 Greenwich
street, was bitten by a spider several
days ago. Ha paid no attention to the
bite until last night, when his left arm
began to swell. At the advice of a friend
he visited the Receiving Hospital, where
Dr. Tormey after an examination, de
clared that he was suffering from blood
poisoning. It is not unlikely that the un
fortunate man will lose his arm as the
result of the deadly bite.
Reese told the doctor that he was en
gaged in making some repairs about his
home when the Insect bit him. He felt
a stinging pain In his arm, but thinking
it would pass away, he paid little atten
tion to It.
GORTER THROWN IN JAIL.
The Inventor of the Water Tower
Charged With Defrauding A. S.
Paree.
W. H. Gorther, the inventor of the
water tower that is in use in the Fire
Department, was arrested last night on
a warrant from Police Court 4 charging
him with a violation of the State law
relative to leaving the State with intent
to defraud his creditors.
The complaining witness is A. S. Paree,
a ciVil engineer. Some time ago Paree
sued Gorter for preparing the plans of
the water tower and was awarded $250 by
a jury in Judge Hunt's court. Gorter, it
is claimed, refused to pay the judgment,
and Paree. learning that he wast about
to leave for Alaska last night, visited
police headquarters and swore out a war
rant for his arrest. Gorter denied that he
owed Paree any money, and threatened
to make it interesting for him after his
case is disposed of.

ALLEGED EMBEZZLER
WANTED AT MARTINEZ.
Charles B. Jones Accused of Having
Defrauded a District
Attorney-
MARTINEZ. May 13.â Charles R. Jones,
well known In Martinez, Crockett and
Oakland, and at one time traveling agent
of the Renters Co-operative Investment
Company of San Francisco, is a fugitive
from justice. He is wanted on a charge
of embezzlement, preferred by District
Attorney Brown, and for beating the
landlord of the Hotel Crockett out of
For some time Jones has been at Crock
ett placing loan.s. He often came to Mar
tinez and did business here. It is a rule
of the company that no money is to ba
received by* an agen.t from any person
applying for a loan, but it seems Jones
violated this rule while in Martinez. At
torney Brown, in doing business for cli
ents, asked for a loan, and Jones first
collected $50 from him. Since that tlmÂ«
Brown has not seen man' nor money.
Cheaper Electric Power.
MARYSVILLE. May 13.â An experiment
concluded here by Dr. F. A. C. Perrine of
Stanford University utilizing the electri
cal power line of the Yuba Power Com
pany from its power house to Browns
Valley, a distance of ten miles, demon
strated that 36,000 volts may be transmit
ted over a copper wire, using glass insu
lation, against sixteen thousand, which
has been the maximum in power trans
mission heretofore. The result of the ex
periment will be to effect a saving of half
in the cost of wire in the construction of
electrical transmission plants in the fu
ture. As it is now the cost of wire is
about half the entire cost of the plant.
